  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_23d6b474-6d1d-4e9b-82fa-ee538c2f65b1'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<span id="freeTextContainer14033506363723054965"><blockquote> <p> Una obra al tiempo emotiva y escrita en el tono irónico y apasionado que caracteriza a la autora, en la que nos entrega la suma de sus días como mujer y como escritora </p> </blockquote> <p> En las páginas de este libro, Isabel Allende narra con franqueza la historia reciente de su vida y la de su peculiar familia en California, en una casa abierta, llena de gente y de personajes literarios</p></span>
  <span id="freeText14033506363723054965" style="display:none"><blockquote> <p> Una obra al tiempo emotiva y escrita en el tono irónico y apasionado que caracteriza a la autora, en la que nos entrega la suma de sus días como mujer y como escritora </p> </blockquote> <p> En las páginas de este libro, Isabel Allende narra con franqueza la historia reciente de su vida y la de su peculiar familia en California, en una casa abierta, llena de gente y de personajes literarios, y protegida por un espíritu: hijas perdidas, nietos y libros que nacen, éxitos y dolores, un viaje al mundo de las adicciones y otros a lugares remotos del mundo en busca de inspiración, junto a divorcios, encuentros, amores, separaciones, crisis de pareja y reconciliaciones. También es una historia de amor entre un hombre y una mujer maduros, que han salvado juntos muchos escollos sin perder ni la pasión ni el humor, y de una familia moderna, desgarrada por conflictos y unida, a pesar de todo, por el cariño y la decisión de salir adelante. Esta es la familia que descubrimos en <i>Paula</i> y que desciende de los personajes de <i>La Casa de los Espíritus</i>. </p></span>
  <a data-text-id="14033506363723054965" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_1578210805" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1578210805" />
    <a title="Brina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2933855-brina"><img alt="Brina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601675085p2/2933855.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1578210805?book_show_action=true">Mar 13, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brina" href="/user/show/2933855-brina">Brina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780061551833" href="/book/show/1991383.The_Sum_of_Our_Days">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2933855-brina?shelf=memoirs">memoirs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2933855-brina?shelf=hispanic-culture">hispanic-culture</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2933855-brina?shelf=isabel-allende">isabel-allende</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1578210805" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10687128625460454354">Isabel Allende has been my favorite author since I read House of the Spirits for the first time twenty years ago. I have read many of her other novels including Daughter of Fortune and Portrait in Sepia as well as Ines of My Soul. Just last month I devoured The Japanese Lover in a day. Yet, I have never welcomed myself into her life and read one of her nonfiction memoirs, limiting myself to her fiction. <br/><br/>The Sum of Our Days is the memoir Allende dictated to her late daughter Paula over the span o</span>
  <span id="freeText10687128625460454354" style="display:none">Isabel Allende has been my favorite author since I read House of the Spirits for the first time twenty years ago. I have read many of her other novels including Daughter of Fortune and Portrait in Sepia as well as Ines of My Soul. Just last month I devoured The Japanese Lover in a day. Yet, I have never welcomed myself into her life and read one of her nonfiction memoirs, limiting myself to her fiction. <br /><br />The Sum of Our Days is the memoir Allende dictated to her late daughter Paula over the span of 13 years. Allende writes of the pain the family fell into following Paula's death and all of the trials and tribulations that come with being a matriarch of a large, extended clan. Usually author memoirs are of the writing process, and they are included here in passing, but this book read like a novel that only a master storyteller like Allende is capable of telling. <br /><br />In this book we meet all the members of Allende's extended American family as well as some Chilean members. We intimately follow her relationship with her second husband Willie as well as that of her son Nico and his children. Yet despite the achievements that come with being a world renowned writer, all Allende's milestones flow back to Paula and the measure of time in reference to when her daughter passed away. Willie has allowed Allende to come out of the most dismal period of her life and the two venture into the least likely of relationships, resulting in marriage. Along the way we meet the cast of characters in Allende's life, each playing a distinct role enriching each other's days. <br /><br />In spite of living her youth in a Catholic country, Allende does not view herself as Catholic, but a spiritualist. Willie has constructed for her an actual House of the Spirits on a hilltop overlooking San Francisco Bay. The extended clan lives in the same neighborhood and many memories occur at her abuela's actual table of the spirits imported from Chile. Allende uses the table along with astrological signs to predict all that has happened to her family during the period encompassed in this memoir, including births, deaths, and the subjects of her next books. As I had already read a number of Allende's novels, I found her system for choosing subject matter to be a fascinating endeavor. <br /> <br />Isabel Allende could write enduring prose based on anything she even witnessed in passing. Writing on what she knows the most intimately allows for effortless and nearly flawless prose even in translation. I feel that after this book I have come to know her and her family better and now reading her books feels like meeting with an old friend rather than a famous author. As always I look forward to when I can curl up with her novels and memoirs. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10687128625460454354" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Here, too, are the amazing stories behind Allende’s books, the superstitions that guide her writing process, and her adventurous travels. <div id="review_20944159" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/20944159" />
    <a title="Natalie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/786079-natalie"><img alt="Natalie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1201626234p2/786079.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/20944159?book_show_action=true">Apr 24, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Natalie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Natalie" href="/user/show/786079-natalie">Natalie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780061551833" href="/book/show/1991383.The_Sum_of_Our_Days">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer20944159" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer838519572512083261">This is a sweet and absorbing compendium of the goings-on in Allende's family in the years since her daughter's death. Though it recounts heartaches and sadnesses, the overall tone is wry and upbeat. It's really just a tale of life in a kooky but loving extended family, with emotions and ups-and-downs that a lot of us can relate to--not the specific events, of course, but the general feelings. Not that many of us take regular trips to the Amazon or India, have a daughter-in-law come out of the c</span>
  <span id="freeText838519572512083261" style="display:none">This is a sweet and absorbing compendium of the goings-on in Allende's family in the years since her daughter's death. Though it recounts heartaches and sadnesses, the overall tone is wry and upbeat. It's really just a tale of life in a kooky but loving extended family, with emotions and ups-and-downs that a lot of us can relate to--not the specific events, of course, but the general feelings. Not that many of us take regular trips to the Amazon or India, have a daughter-in-law come out of the closet after 3 children and move in with your stepson's fiance, or go on a four-day drug-induced hallucination. But the desire to create a family circle, the daily irritations of marriage, the grief that sneaks up on you, the sorrow of not being able to remove others' pain, these common emotions are what draw you in to this very personal work. Allende is open with her grief and fear, and self-deprecating with her humor.<br /><br />Having heard her read from the book when it came out made a big difference in how I read. I would have enjoyed it anyway, but more of the dry sense of humor came through when I imagined it in her voice, much the same way as I experience reading David Sedaris. (I can't believe I'm comparing Isabel Allende to David Sedaris, but there it is.) At any rate, it is a pleasant and absorbing read, whether or not you have read any of her novels (though you may have a better sense of her if you've read some of her other work).</span>
  <a data-text-id="838519572512083261" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_61665988" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/61665988" />
    <a title="Laura" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/82840-laura"><img alt="Laura" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1465057364p2/82840.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/61665988?book_show_action=true">Jun 30, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura" href="/user/show/82840-laura">Laura</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer61665988" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16992904553567757487">This is Allende's second memoir, and she writes it to her daughter, Paula, who died maybe about 10 years earlier. It is an account of everything that has happened in Allende's family since Paula's death. As it is a memoir, clearly, it reads very differently from Allende's typical saga stories. The narrative arc, following the day to day events of life, is not always so smooth, naturally. What I really loved about this memoir is Allende's ability to talk openly about some of the deepest pains in </span>
  <span id="freeText16992904553567757487" style="display:none">This is Allende's second memoir, and she writes it to her daughter, Paula, who died maybe about 10 years earlier. It is an account of everything that has happened in Allende's family since Paula's death. As it is a memoir, clearly, it reads very differently from Allende's typical saga stories. The narrative arc, following the day to day events of life, is not always so smooth, naturally. What I really loved about this memoir is Allende's ability to talk openly about some of the deepest pains in her life and in the life of her family. She is not one for melodrama, not at all... instead, she has a talent for getting right to the heart of the matter and describing it with compassionate precision. I admire this ability greatly, as I find it very difficult to write clearly and truly sincerely about some of the most painful moments in my own life. Allende does it with such ease and such beauty that it inspires me to write more and try harder to really say what has happened in my own life without any pretensions or ideas of how it "should" sound. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16992904553567757487" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_813522101" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/813522101" />
    <a title="Alina Colleen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27375066-alina-colleen"><img alt="Alina Colleen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1602117380p2/27375066.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/813522101?book_show_action=true">Jan 05, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alina Colleen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alina Colleen" href="/user/show/27375066-alina-colleen">Alina Colleen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780061551833" href="/book/show/1991383.The_Sum_of_Our_Days">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer813522101" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15885850631037523572">If I were feeling charitable I would give this memoir three stars, but since the book ended with a TMI scene in which Isabel and her elderly husband get naked together in a jacuzzi and she asserts her "non-feminist" love for him, I won't. It's a shame that this is the first Allende book I've read, because now I'm not sure if her fiction is any good. Based on the meandering nature and average prose of this memoir, my guess is not really, but maybe I'll still give The House of the Spirits a go sin</span>
  <span id="freeText15885850631037523572" style="display:none">If I were feeling charitable I would give this memoir three stars, but since the book ended with a TMI scene in which Isabel and her elderly husband get naked together in a jacuzzi and she asserts her "non-feminist" love for him, I won't. It's a shame that this is the first Allende book I've read, because now I'm not sure if her fiction is any good. Based on the meandering nature and average prose of this memoir, my guess is not really, but maybe I'll still give The House of the Spirits a go since Isabel wrote it when she was younger (and presumably less pompous). <br /><br />Most people who write memoirs do so, I feel, because they have a compelling or unique life story to tell. Usually these seem to involve poor or usual childhoods, which the author reflects on with humor. That or a celebrity pays a journalist to wrangle their scattered recollections into something resembling complete sentences. But Isabel is not a celebrity, at least not in the traditional sense; although she is doubtless extraordinarily wealthy, she leads a very normal, family-centered life, which does not exactly make for an engrossing plot. Some people have the gift of making the ordinary seem more interesting than it is, but such is not the case with Allende. Nor does she have any particularly sagacious advice to offer, or opinions that stray from beyond the realm of normalcy. She really wants you to know that she hates George Bush, for example, but so did a lot of people, and Allende's logic for doing so is neither unique nor particularly analytical. So, really, don't read this unless you already like Allende and want to know what her spoiled life in California is like. Oh, and who each of her children marry, and which grandchild she considers the most attractive. <br /><br />After reading this memoir, I feel like Isabel Allede is maybe not as good of a person as she thinks she is. She repeatedly refers to herself as the matriarch of her "tribe" (and I have always found it distasteful to use that word outside of its anthropological definition), and meddles endlessly in her children's, stepchildren's, and various daughter- and son-in-law's affairs. Her daughter, Paula, dies from porphyria-related complications near the beginning of the book, but Allende has already written a second, separate memoir about that time (entitled, you guessed it, "Paula"). With the proceeds from the memoir about her daughter, Allende establishes a charitable foundation to help women and children after going on a trip to India and meeting a desperately impoverished woman who tries to give her baby daughter to Allende. Isabel never says what the name of this foundation is, though, and it's unclear what the foundation does (though Allende, in a typical show of nepotism, hires her daughter-in-law to run the foundation). She also gives her remaining offspring, Nico, a house, and frequently describes how attractive he is and how lucky any girl would be to have him as a husband (eew). She gives money and employment to various members of the close and extended family, which is cool in one way I guess, and also a bit disturbing and cloying in another (to what extent do her relatives view her primarily as a source of funds?) <br /><br />Isabel also engages in a fair amount of body-shaming, which is not an attractive quality especially in a middle-aged woman of considerable means. She constantly harps on about how short she is; as a short person myself, I can assure you it's not that bad. At one point she describes how she teeters around on high heels and must cling to her husband's arm for support, and then later in the memoir she claims to be low-maintenance. She often observes that she is "no beauty", but from the few photos of her that I've seen online, Allende is not exactly unattractive. Isabel claims not to place a great deal of importance on physical beauty, as evidenced by the fact that all of the heroines in her books are "strong women" who cannot simply glide through life on looks alone. In reality, however, Allende's modus operandi is to surround herself with beautiful people. She decides that Lori, with her "model-like" figure, is a suitable match for her son Nico. She incorporates a gorgeous Greek-American woman (unrelated by blood or marriage), Juliette, and her two sons into her tribe and provides said "Aphrodite" with a job as her assistant. And she is constantly claiming that her husband, Willie, looks like Paul Newman, in a seemingly congratulatory aside to herself for snagging such an attractive partner. <br /><br />The most cringeworthy part of the book, though, is probably her handling of Celia's story. Celia, an opinionated Venezuelan, was Nico's first wife and mother to Isabel's three grandchildren. After giving birth for the third time in almost as few years, Celia descends into a depression and eventually concludes that she is gay. She tells Nico, who says he has been betrayed, and decides that they must divorce. Isabel is outraged. She seems to blame Celia for causing discord in her family, and instead of being understanding, Nico asks Isabel to sever all communications with Celia. Allende recounts these developments in a dramatic fashion, and never concedes that Celia's oppressive Catholic upbringing might explain why she was not able to acknowledge her homosexuality until the age of 27. The Celia/Nico story takes up a large chunk of the book, and Isabel often remarks how embarrassing the entire episode was for the family. It is almost as though she takes a perverse pleasure in the gossip and drama the episode created. I found it distasteful that Allende would make this one of the primary plot elements in her memoir, as it seemed exploitative rather than essential. <br /><br />Once Isabel has accumulated some money from her book sales, she and her husband purchase a large plot of land and build a custom house for themselves. She becomes, in her own words, a castellana: Mistress of the Castle. She goes on a trip to the Amazon. She takes her grandchildren on safari in Kenya. She has a heated pool installed. You know, rich people stuff. None of this would be so bad, perhaps, if she recounted it in an interesting way, but there is a cozy, almost cloying quality to Allende's writing. I thought at first it might be a fault of the translation, but Isabel herself asserts that she checked the English version before it was approved for publication. She seems to think her readers will find it interesting that she has sexual fantasies about Antonio Banderas, or that she helps her husband's accountant select a mail-order bride from China. She comes across as a meddling matriarch - something she herself acknowledges - and seems to be unduly proud of her status as castellana. She is simply not a person who I relate to very well, and I couldn't figure out why she cares about half of the things she did. Some might chalk this up to cultural differences and the importance that Chileans place on family, but Isabel's interest in her tribe seems to spring from a need to control others. Besides, it's not necessarily about the quantity of family you have surrounding you, but rather the quality and character of your familial relationships, which should be mutual acceptance, not judgement. <br /><br />Oh well. I'll try House of Spirits and nothing else. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15885850631037523572" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1353175505?book_show_action=true">Aug 03, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chana" href="/user/show/1400289-chana">Chana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780061551833" href="/book/show/1991383.The_Sum_of_Our_Days">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1400289-chana?shelf=memoirs-and-biographies">memoirs-and-biographies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1400289-chana?shelf=california">california</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1353175505" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11728654208209644372">I liked House of Spirits very much. This? Well this is a memoir, written some years after the death of her daughter Paula. It is sometimes written in the form of a dialogue with Paula. It has the feel of confession, apology and regret; not uncommon in memoirs written in later life. But Isabel Allende is such a firebrand, such a fighter, a real spitfire that she doesn't sink into it. She basically calls up her tough attitude and gathers her family and imposes both her will and her intense love to</span>
  <span id="freeText11728654208209644372" style="display:none">I liked House of Spirits very much. This? Well this is a memoir, written some years after the death of her daughter Paula. It is sometimes written in the form of a dialogue with Paula. It has the feel of confession, apology and regret; not uncommon in memoirs written in later life. But Isabel Allende is such a firebrand, such a fighter, a real spitfire that she doesn't sink into it. She basically calls up her tough attitude and gathers her family and imposes both her will and her intense love to do her best to keep everyone together. <br />As an author she can be very funny, but she is also a bereaved parent and that unbearable sorrow runs through the book like an underground river, occasionally surfacing but mostly just below the surface of Isabel's personality and writing.<br />I can't say I enjoyed reading it as much as her fiction. Everyone's life is somewhat boring to other people unless it is written in the form of entertainment. Isabel is entertaining, but she is also explaining, confessing and purging. The best part of this book is Willie, her husband. Their love story is beautiful, a real story of love and hope, not a youthful fairy tale, but a real love of life, pain and age. At the end I felt it was a memoir of the beauty, fragility and durability of love.</span>

<div id="review_1244636964" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1244636964" />

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1244636964" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6443110093466901543">Isabel Allende's memoir is a conversation with her daughter Paula, who she lost years before to a hereditary disease. Allende lives in a huge tribe of a family that includes step-children, grandchildren, a Buddhist lesbian couple, and her extended family from Chile. Allende presents herself warts and all, as the mother-in-law from hell. At times, her actions make perfect sense to me and other times I can't believe how much she interferes. I forgive her for most of her faults, but there are some </span>
  <span id="freeText6443110093466901543" style="display:none">Isabel Allende's memoir is a conversation with her daughter Paula, who she lost years before to a hereditary disease. Allende lives in a huge tribe of a family that includes step-children, grandchildren, a Buddhist lesbian couple, and her extended family from Chile. Allende presents herself warts and all, as the mother-in-law from hell. At times, her actions make perfect sense to me and other times I can't believe how much she interferes. I forgive her for most of her faults, but there are some that involve deception I am less inclined to do so. She talks about the writing of a number of her books and her writing rituals. She provides insights into what it is like for a person from another culture to make her American family more like a Chilean family. She is deeply honest and even when her story delves into sadness and tragedy, I never felt it was depressing. She has a passion for life which shines through and undoubtedly is what keeps her going.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6443110093466901543" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer13497360487570287261">Wow, what a rollicking read. I kept having to remind myself that this was a memoir and not one of Allende's novels. Lesser women would have crawled into a hole having lived through the tragedy and day to day uproar of her life, but Isabel Allende just keeps drawing the hurt and struggling into her family circle and that extended family supports each other and moves forward together.   <span id="freeText13497360487570287261" style="display:none">Wow, what a rollicking read. I kept having to remind myself that this was a memoir and not one of Allende's novels. Lesser women would have crawled into a hole having lived through the tragedy and day to day uproar of her life, but Isabel Allende just keeps drawing the hurt and struggling into her family circle and that extended family supports each other and moves forward together. She is truly a matriarch who, as she admits, sometimes needs to be reined in a bit.<br /><br />Sometimes she needs to reach outside the family for support. That is when the "sisters of disorder" step in.<br /><br />"Though I had just met her, I told her what was happening with you.<br />"We are going to pray for your daughter and for you", she told me. A<br />month later she invited me to her 'prayer circle,' and that is how<br />these new friends came to accompany me during your agony and death...<br />and continue to comfort me today. For me it is a sisterhood sealed in<br />heaven. Every woman in this world should have such a circle of<br />friends. Each of us is witness to the others; lives; we keep secrets,<br />help in difficulties, share experiences, and stay in almost daily<br />contact by e-mail. However far I may be traveling, I always have my<br />lie to terra firma: my sisters of disorder."<br /><br />This book is a testament to the power of love of every kind. It is a gift to read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13497360487570287261" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_528126787" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/528126787" />
    <a title="Karen Germain" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/72310-karen-germain"><img alt="Karen Germain" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1441123935p2/72310.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/528126787?book_show_action=true">Feb 06, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Karen Germain" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Karen Germain" href="/user/show/72310-karen-germain">Karen Germain</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer528126787" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18303577696551694677">Since discovering her novels in high school, Isabel Allende has remained one of my favorite authors. Her personal life, is just as entertaining and dramatic as those of her fictional characters. "The Sum of Our Days" is her second memoir, detailing family events following the death of her daughter Paula, whom she wrote about in her first memoir, aptly titled "Paula". <br/><br/>Allende never fails to be interesting and her family proves to be a colorful bunch of characters. Despite a myriad of problems (re</span>
  <span id="freeText18303577696551694677" style="display:none">Since discovering her novels in high school, Isabel Allende has remained one of my favorite authors. Her personal life, is just as entertaining and dramatic as those of her fictional characters. "The Sum of Our Days" is her second memoir, detailing family events following the death of her daughter Paula, whom she wrote about in her first memoir, aptly titled "Paula". <br /><br />Allende never fails to be interesting and her family proves to be a colorful bunch of characters. Despite a myriad of problems (really, what family is problem free?) Allende presents a group of people who love each other fiercely and whom freely embrace bringing new friends into their fold. Their home in San Francisco is a warm place for anyone in need and it is impossible not to fall in love with their family. Allende writes about her family and friends in such a caring way, that I connected with each person.​<br /><br />Allende isn't shoving tips or life lessons down the readers throat, but in a subtle way, she gives a lot of great advice regarding marriage and relationships. The relationship advice extending not just to significant others, but includes children and friends. She has made mistakes and candidly reveals them in this memoir, forcing the reader to be introspective about their own relationships and mistakes. ​Allende's vulnerability makes her so accessible. <br /><br />I finished this book, still a huge fan of her writing, but I also wished that I could be part of her family. You know that game where you pick five people that you would want to have as a dinner guest? Allende makes my list. ​<br /><br />This book is a must for Allende fans, but would also be a great independent memoir read for someone who is completely unfamiliar with her novels. It stands on its own, although I would recommend reading "Paula" first​, as there are many references to it and the two memoirs are really companion books.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18303577696551694677" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3131238-judy?shelf=chile">chile</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3131238-judy?shelf=bio-memoir">bio-memoir</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3131238-judy?shelf=california">california</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer362982913" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9869361088669597281">I picked this book up on a whim from my local used bookstore mostly because its difficult to find biographies/memoirs for people about people who don't have a twitter following or those who create sensational headlines. In hindsight, I'm surprised I bought it because I wasn't blown away by the one book I had read by the author,<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7005479.Island_Beneath_the_Sea' title='Island Beneath the Sea by Isabel Allende' rel='nofollow noopener'>Island Beneath the Sea</a>.<br/><br/>I'm glad I did purchase it. Allende's candor and colorfulness swept me away. Upon finishing this book, I read her first bestseller, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9328.The_House_of_the_Spirits' title='The House of the Spirits by Isabel Allende' rel='nofollow noopener'>The House of the</a></span>
  <span id="freeText9869361088669597281" style="display:none">I picked this book up on a whim from my local used bookstore mostly because its difficult to find biographies/memoirs for people about people who don't have a twitter following or those who create sensational headlines. In hindsight, I'm surprised I bought it because I wasn't blown away by the one book I had read by the author,<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7005479.Island_Beneath_the_Sea" title="Island Beneath the Sea by Isabel Allende" rel="nofollow noopener">Island Beneath the Sea</a>.<br /><br />I'm glad I did purchase it. Allende's candor and colorfulness swept me away. Upon finishing this book, I read her first bestseller, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9328.The_House_of_the_Spirits" title="The House of the Spirits by Isabel Allende" rel="nofollow noopener">The House of the Spirits</a>, and enjoyed how much her personality seeps through the pages. <br /><br />The drama in Allende's actual life reflects in her written work. I appreciate her non-fiction more than her fiction works and have put <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24790.Paula" title="Paula by Isabel Allende" rel="nofollow noopener">Paula</a> on my list to read.</span>

  <span id="freeText11497138442217399228" style="display:none">It was really interesting to meet Isabel Allende though this book. This was my first one, actually. It has inspired me to look up more of her novels. It can work both ways - you could get to this book after reading her other novels and find a new perspective on things, or you can use this one to give you insight and prepare the scene for reading her other works. I enjoyed reading it in Spanish - with some difficulty as I don't speak the langauge very well, but it was well worth it. What started as a language experiment on my part ended up being a beautiful journey getting to know Allende's tribe and life.</span>

    <a title="Julie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/632373-julie"><img alt="Julie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546351831p2/632373.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/26674590?book_show_action=true">Jul 08, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julie" href="/user/show/632373-julie">Julie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780061551833" href="/book/show/1991383.The_Sum_of_Our_Days">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer26674590" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16076925888552301937">The Sum of Our Days is the gorgeous and quirky third memoir by renowned Chilean-American writer Isabel Allende, translated from her native Spanish into English. Her memoir, Paula, was a stunningly intimate reflection on the loss of her young, 28-year-old daughter. My Invented Country was her tribute to her home country, spanning the assassination of her uncle Salvador in the September 11, 1973 coup and the 9/11 attacks on her adopted country. Now, she weaves the tale of building a quirky extende</span>
  <span id="freeText16076925888552301937" style="display:none">The Sum of Our Days is the gorgeous and quirky third memoir by renowned Chilean-American writer Isabel Allende, translated from her native Spanish into English. Her memoir, Paula, was a stunningly intimate reflection on the loss of her young, 28-year-old daughter. My Invented Country was her tribute to her home country, spanning the assassination of her uncle Salvador in the September 11, 1973 coup and the 9/11 attacks on her adopted country. Now, she weaves the tale of building a quirky extended family and continuing to live with her daughter’s absence.<br /><br />The family faces a variety of transformative events, including drug addiction, illness and disease, new heterosexual and lesbian relationships, and grandchildren. Allende also reminisces about her travels and writing, and shares a portrait of a marriage strengthened by time and trial. Even when Allende becomes the dominating family matriarch, she remains likeable. I attribute it to her rare skill in crafting a brazenly honest memoir; few memoirists seem as willing to show their biases and missteps as Allende. Her reflections on motherhood, addiction, feminism, and more pepper the book. These elements coalesce and sum up Allende’s adventurously- and skillfully-led life so far. <br />–Review by Julie Fiandt<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16076925888552301937" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer15985449375060048525">While I was reading the first 30 pages or so I kept thinking that I would LOVE this book. I did not love this book. I felt really tainted or something while reading it; or maybe like I was being force fed. I think I felt that way because it was far too new age for me. Typically, I'm someone who can appreciate new age "wisdom," but I could not in this book and I think it's because of the harsh light she put it in. Plus, she's a meddling new ager; which really rubs me the wrong way. I think more t</span>
  <span id="freeText15985449375060048525" style="display:none">While I was reading the first 30 pages or so I kept thinking that I would LOVE this book. I did not love this book. I felt really tainted or something while reading it; or maybe like I was being force fed. I think I felt that way because it was far too new age for me. Typically, I'm someone who can appreciate new age "wisdom," but I could not in this book and I think it's because of the harsh light she put it in. Plus, she's a meddling new ager; which really rubs me the wrong way. I think more than anything her meddling in everyone's life was the thing that I could not get over in this book; despite the extreme drama going on throughout. I was impressed that she was so honest about her meddling and being a nightmare mother-in-law. <br /><br />Also, the "magic"...I've really never been a fantasy reader or into magic, hence why I don't think I would ever enjoy the Harry Potter books. Maybe, I'm just really lacking in imagination, but I think reality and heartfelt emotions are far more beautiful than anything magic can offer. <br /><br />That said, there were little words of wisdom throughout that I appreciated and I thought it was very awesome that throughout all the drama their little "tribe" was able to work through it and stick together. Also, I enjoyed the writing style a lot!</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13572235028343060405"><p>What seems at first a series of short chapters filled with spicy anecdotes and gossipy chitchat proves instead a powerful meditation on the meaning of life and love. Nearly all the critics remarked that this engaging memoir packs as much suspense and drama as any of Allende's novels. ("Allende seems to have no concept of what might be called boundaries," says the <em>Washington Post</em>.) Allende's warm, friendly tone creates a highly personal and poignant narrative, filled with wisdom and humor. Critic</p></span>
  <span id="freeText13572235028343060405" style="display:none"><p>What seems at first a series of short chapters filled with spicy anecdotes and gossipy chitchat proves instead a powerful meditation on the meaning of life and love. Nearly all the critics remarked that this engaging memoir packs as much suspense and drama as any of Allende's novels. ("Allende seems to have no concept of what might be called boundaries," says the <em>Washington Post</em>.) Allende's warm, friendly tone creates a highly personal and poignant narrative, filled with wisdom and humor. Critics agreed that, when compared to the haunting <em>Paula</em>, "one of the most moving books ever written about grief" (<em>USA Today</em>), <em>The Sum of Our Days</em> regrettably comes up short, lacking the emotional immediacy of its predecessor despite Allende's dazzling storytelling abilities. The <em>Washington Post </em>also criticized a lack of deeper self-analysis on Allende's part. Nevertheless, <em>Sum</em> is an eloquent addition to Allende's work</p><p>This is an excerpt from a review published in <a href="http://www.bookmarksmagazine.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Bookmarks magazine</a>.</p></span>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2550155379?book_show_action=true">Oct 04, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mia" href="/user/show/63107087-mia">Mia</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780061551833" href="/book/show/1991383.The_Sum_of_Our_Days">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2550155379" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13968742913252778225">Isabel Allende has allowed all of us to see her desperate need to control the lives of every one around her and her incredible sense of entitlement. She has gone through much political and personal upheaval in her life, which may help to explain her control issues. It is harder to understand why she thinks it is OK to keep a key to the house of her son, rearrange furniture, walk in without knocking on the door, and show herself to be the most overbearing and impossible mother-in-law ever. Later </span>
  <span id="freeText13968742913252778225" style="display:none">Isabel Allende has allowed all of us to see her desperate need to control the lives of every one around her and her incredible sense of entitlement. She has gone through much political and personal upheaval in her life, which may help to explain her control issues. It is harder to understand why she thinks it is OK to keep a key to the house of her son, rearrange furniture, walk in without knocking on the door, and show herself to be the most overbearing and impossible mother-in-law ever. Later she decides to try to buy an unborn twin from the surrogate mother carrying the twins for a childless couple so her son and his wife can have a child. Truly a monstrous idea. She has an active belief in a spiritual life and often sees evidence of her daughter with her. The book is framed as a letter to her child. This is a very sad book about an elderly woman carrying many burdens of sorrow. <br /><br />I had read several of her books and her personal story seems a piece with her fiction.</span>

<div id="review_1462106108" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1462106108" />
    <a title="Teri Reck" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31657066-teri-reck"><img alt="Teri Reck" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1462106108?book_show_action=true">Dec 06, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Teri Reck" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Teri Reck" href="/user/show/31657066-teri-reck">Teri Reck</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780061551833" href="/book/show/1991383.The_Sum_of_Our_Days">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1462106108" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12597388041645286680">Isabel once again opens her home and heart and family to the scrutiny of her readers. She lives seemingly a thousand lifetimes worth of anguishes, sorrows, defeats, and finally joys. In this memoir, she writes of her life after her daughter, Paula, had died an untimely death. As though, that event in her life weren't painful enough, the years following were also filled with other pains and sorrows that seem to be as devastating as death. But somehow she gathers her family, her tribe, to herself </span>
  <span id="freeText12597388041645286680" style="display:none">Isabel once again opens her home and heart and family to the scrutiny of her readers. She lives seemingly a thousand lifetimes worth of anguishes, sorrows, defeats, and finally joys. In this memoir, she writes of her life after her daughter, Paula, had died an untimely death. As though, that event in her life weren't painful enough, the years following were also filled with other pains and sorrows that seem to be as devastating as death. But somehow she gathers her family, her tribe, to herself and challenge by challenge, she perseveres. Through all of it she gains strength and wisdom. And she survives. I am now going to go on another of my author journeys, and I will read, or re-read since I have read almost all her of her books already, her body of work which will continue for a good long time as she starts a new book every Jan. 8th.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12597388041645286680" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_70119216" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/70119216" />
    <a title="Fernanda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1086377-fernanda"><img alt="Fernanda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1451875852p2/1086377.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/70119216?book_show_action=true">Sep 04, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Fernanda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Fernanda" href="/user/show/1086377-fernanda">Fernanda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer70119216" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9164960432502566815">I was surprised to find myself reading a memoir which reads like a women's magazine article (we have such magazine in Latin America, and I now think she writes the Tía Eulogia articles), not like the memoirs of a serious/acclaimed writer. I had read "Eva Luna" and "Cuentos de Eva Luna" before and had fallen in love with her powerful work... This book, unfortunately, lacks that character. It's like listening to my aunts telling stories about my family, which I know are 10% truth. It's all gossip.</span>
  <span id="freeText9164960432502566815" style="display:none">I was surprised to find myself reading a memoir which reads like a women's magazine article (we have such magazine in Latin America, and I now think she writes the Tía Eulogia articles), not like the memoirs of a serious/acclaimed writer. I had read "Eva Luna" and "Cuentos de Eva Luna" before and had fallen in love with her powerful work... This book, unfortunately, lacks that character. It's like listening to my aunts telling stories about my family, which I know are 10% truth. It's all gossip. The famous "clan" is, many times, unbelievable. And it gives the idea she not often takes people around her seriously. I liked it though, but it's not her best...</span>
  <a data-text-id="9164960432502566815" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_839182465" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/839182465" />
    <a title="Lil" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/777724-lil"><img alt="Lil" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1449019046p2/777724.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/839182465?book_show_action=true">Jan 30, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lil" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lil" href="/user/show/777724-lil">Lil</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780061551833" href="/book/show/1991383.The_Sum_of_Our_Days">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Lil by: </span>
      Cesar Kanamori
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/777724-lil?shelf=reading-from-home-2014">reading-from-home-2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/777724-lil?shelf=2014-loaned-recommended-or-given">2014-loaned-recommended-or-given</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer839182465" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8757057908219038570">This is the follow up to Allende's powerful memoir of grief, Paula. She's writing to Paula about the family events over about ten years after Paula's passing and the result is much more interesting than you would think. While Allende's family has more drama than some (or most?), the heart of this book is really the love of the family, through good times and bad. Strikingly honest, surprisingly compelling. I cried at the last words of Abuela Hilda (you'll have to read it yourself). Read this, but</span>
  <span id="freeText8757057908219038570" style="display:none">This is the follow up to Allende's powerful memoir of grief, Paula. She's writing to Paula about the family events over about ten years after Paula's passing and the result is much more interesting than you would think. While Allende's family has more drama than some (or most?), the heart of this book is really the love of the family, through good times and bad. Strikingly honest, surprisingly compelling. I cried at the last words of Abuela Hilda (you'll have to read it yourself). Read this, but only after reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24790.Paula" title="Paula by Isabel Allende" rel="nofollow noopener">Paula</a>. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8757057908219038570" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('JAyO27uTT1euKMLBparTxPgdqrp1WIxpfJBajvedYQ3LlVWplfoUr0ZUk8ljIvoT4JcDjMNnrFFPsG//VJNiHQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('DAtx3HaMlVzd/oXT1MBbQfTjUsyv60d7CnlVfwbpmIjjkqquWOXOpDWC1NsSSHKW7Gn7+hnUZ0M5WWAOpeebmA==')})
  }

Salvar el fuego retrata dos Méxicos completamente escindidos uno del otro, donde Marina, que pertenece a la clase social más alta, se vincula con un hombre al extremo de la sociedad. Esta es una novela que retrata las contradicciones de un país y las contradicciones más hondas de la naturaleza humana. Es una novela de amor y es una novela que al final termina por brindar esperanza. «Una novela polifónica que narra con intensidad y con excepcional dinamismo una historia de violencia en el México contemporáneo donde el amor y la redención aún son posibles. El autor se sirve tantode una extraordinaria fuerza visual como de la recreación y reinvención del lenguaje coloquial para lograr una obra de inquietante verosimilitud. Los distintos planos narrativos tienen como hilo conductor el cuerpo humano, motivo de celebración y expuesto a numerosos excesos.»Del acta del jurado La crítica ha dicho:«El mexicano Guillermo Arriaga no es solo un escritor de la gran pantalla sino un narrador de raza, cuyas obsesiones vitales dejan honda huella en el lector.»Matías Néspolo, El Mundo «Un autor absolutamente único.»Guadalupe Nettel «Uno de los autores contemporáneos más potentes, intensos y originales de la literatura en idioma español.»El Exprés (México) «Arriaga demuestra ser gran director a la par que gran escritor.»Roberto Piorno, Guía del Ocio «Con sensibilidad extrema y poderío visual, enlazando con coherencia personajes y situaciones que inicialmente parecen no guardar relación [...], Arriaga demuestra que, además de un espléndido guionista, también es un buen director.»Carlos Boyero, El País «El Salvaje es uno de los mejores libros que he leído, no solo en este sino en los últimos años.»Santiago Gamboa «La presencia ominosa de la muerte; el amor o la pasión que todo lo crea y, por encima, la fuerza irrefrenable de la vida que arrastra todo consigo en su prepotencia arrolladora. Esos son los motivos que entrelaza con sabiduría en El Salvaje, una ambiciosa y lograda novela.»Matías Néspolo, El Mundo «Sublime Arriaga. Esta novela cierra la trilogia Las memorias del Aguila y el Jaguar. Alexander Cold y Nadia Santos se encuentran en este momento, en otra de sus aventuras, aunque en esta ocasion, ellos, la abuela (que se llama Kate Cold) de Alex y el resto de la compania de International Geographic tienen su destino en Africa Ecuatorial con la intencion de hacer un safari en elefante, pero, desde el momento en que una sacerdotisa vudu les previene de un Posible y tragico final, se complican las cosas. Despues de ese acontecimiento, Alex y Nadia deciden ir a la zona de acampada, dado que el dia siguiente les tocaria salir en el safari previsto, y tendrian que preparar sus pertenencias para el viaje. Cuenta la historia de Ofelia, una de las cuatro hermanas Fernández Mollé, una muchacha formal, feliz, a punto de casarse. Pero una tarde su vida cambia abruptamente para convertirse en una maraña de sentimientos encontrados: delicia, inquietud, felicidad, incertidumbre, miedo y mucha culpa. Con grandes vaivenes interiores y a través de difíciles decisiones, se va convirtiendo en una mujer adulta que enfrenta a su propio modo las circunstancias que le han tocado. Un humor que nos recuerda al mejor Cortázar de Historias de cronopios y de famas por sus equívocos, por la deliciosa ambigüedad y sus habituales juegos de palabras.»José Belmonte Serrano, <span id="freeTextContainer17926569275350414055">Isabel Allende Llona is a Chilean-American novelist. Allende, who writes in the "magic realism" tradition, is considered one of the first successful women novelists in Latin America. She has written novels based in part on her own experiences, often focusing on the experiences of women, weaving myth and realism together. She has lectured and done extensive book tours and has taught literature at s</span>
  <span id="freeText17926569275350414055" style="display:none">Isabel Allende Llona is a Chilean-American novelist. Allende, who writes in the "magic realism" tradition, is considered one of the first successful women novelists in Latin America. She has written novels based in part on her own experiences, often focusing on the experiences of women, weaving myth and realism together. She has lectured and done extensive book tours and has taught literature at several US colleges. She currently resides in California with her husband. Allende adopted U.S. citizenship in 2003.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17926569275350414055" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
